<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Food</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Food_(disambiguation)" title="Food (disambiguation)">Food (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Camera-photo.svg"><img alt="Camera-photo.svg" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Camera-photo.svg/40px-Camera-photo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Camera-photo.svg/60px-Camera-photo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Camera-photo.svg/80px-Camera-photo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>contains too many pictures, charts or diagrams for its overall length</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help to <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Food&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by removing or adjusting images in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Images" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Images">Manual of Style on use of images</a>.</span> <small><i>(October 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Good_Food_Display_-_NCI_Visuals_Online.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="2700" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Good_Food_Display_-_NCI_Visuals_Online.jpg/220px-Good_Food_Display_-_NCI_Visuals_Online.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Good_Food_Display_-_NCI_Visuals_Online.jpg/330px-Good_Food_Display_-_NCI_Visuals_Online.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Good_Food_Display_-_NCI_Visuals_Online.jpg/440px-Good_Food_Display_-_NCI_Visuals_Online.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Good_Food_Display_-_NCI_Visuals_Online.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Various foods</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Foods_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1932" data-file-width="1793" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Foods_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Foods_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Foods_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Foods_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Foods_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Foods_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Foods_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Foods from plant sources</div></div></div>
<p><b>Food</b> is any substance<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> consumed to provide nutritional support for an organism. It is usually of <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plant</a> or <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">animal</a> origin, and contains essential <a href="/wiki/Nutrient" title="Nutrient">nutrients</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Carbohydrate" title="Carbohydrate">carbohydrates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fat" title="Fat">fats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protein_(nutrient)" title="Protein (nutrient)">proteins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitamin" title="Vitamin">vitamins</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Mineral_(nutrient)" title="Mineral (nutrient)">minerals</a>. The substance is <a href="/wiki/Ingestion" title="Ingestion">ingested</a> by an <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">organism</a> and assimilated by the organism's <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">cells</a> to provide <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a>, maintain life, or stimulate growth.
</p><p>Historically, <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">humans</a> secured food through two methods: <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunting and gathering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>. Today, the majority of the <a href="/wiki/Food_energy" title="Food energy">food energy</a> required by the ever <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">increasing</a> <a href="/wiki/World_population" title="World population">population of the world</a> is supplied by the <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">food industry</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Food_safety" title="Food safety">Food safety</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">food security</a> are monitored by agencies like the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_for_Food_Protection" title="International Association for Food Protection">International Association for Food Protection</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Resources_Institute" title="World Resources Institute">World Resources Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a>, and <a href="/wiki/International_Food_Information_Council" title="International Food Information Council">International Food Information Council</a>. They address issues such as <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_diversity" title="Biological diversity">biological diversity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nutritional_economics" title="Nutritional economics">nutritional economics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">water supply</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">access to food</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Right_to_food" title="Right to food">right to food</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_right" title="Human right">human right</a> derived from the <a href="/wiki/International_Covenant_on_Economic,_Social_and_Cultural_Rights" title="International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights">International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICESCR" title="ICESCR">ICESCR</a>), recognizing the "<a href="/wiki/Right_to_an_adequate_standard_of_living" title="Right to an adequate standard of living">right to an adequate standard of living</a>, including adequate food", as well as the "fundamental right to be free from <a href="/wiki/Hunger" title="Hunger">hunger</a>".
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_sources">Food sources</span></h2>
<p>Most food has its origin in plants. Some food is obtained directly from plants; but even animals that are used as food sources are raised by feeding them food derived from plants. <a href="/wiki/Cereal" title="Cereal">Cereal</a> grain is a <a href="/wiki/Staple_food" title="Staple food">staple food</a> that provides more food energy worldwide than any other type of crop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">Corn (maize)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> – in all of their varieties – account for 87% of all grain production worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prodstat_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-prodstat-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Most of the grain that is produced worldwide is fed to livestock.
</p><p>Some foods not from animal or plant sources include various edible <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fungi" title="Fungi">fungi</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Mushroom" title="Mushroom">mushrooms</a>. Fungi and ambient <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">bacteria</a> are used in the preparation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fermentation_(food)" title="Fermentation (food)">fermented</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pickled" title="Pickled">pickled</a> foods like <a href="/wiki/Baker%27s_yeast" title="Baker's yeast">leavened</a> <a href="/wiki/Bread" title="Bread">bread</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcoholic_drinks" title="Alcoholic drinks">alcoholic drinks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheese" title="Cheese">cheese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pickled_cucumber" title="Pickled cucumber">pickles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kombucha" title="Kombucha">kombucha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yogurt" title="Yogurt">yogurt</a>. Another example is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue-green_algae" title="Blue-green algae">blue-green algae</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Spirulina_(dietary_supplement)" title="Spirulina (dietary supplement)">Spirulina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Inorganic substances such as <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">salt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sodium_bicarbonate" title="Sodium bicarbonate">baking soda</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Potassium_hydrogen_tartrate" title="Potassium hydrogen tartrate">cream of tartar</a> are used to preserve or chemically alter an ingredient.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plants">Plants</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Herb" title="Herb">Herb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">spice</a></div>
<p>Many plants and plant parts are eaten as food and around 2,000 plant species are cultivated for food. Many of these plant species have several distinct <a href="/wiki/Cultivar" title="Cultivar">cultivars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Seed" title="Seed">Seeds</a> of plants are a good source of food for animals, including humans, because they contain the nutrients necessary for the plant's initial growth, including many healthful fats, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Omega-3" title="Omega-3">omega fats</a>. In fact, the majority of food consumed by human beings are seed-based foods. Edible seeds include cereals (<a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Et_cetera" title="Et cetera">et cetera</a>), <a href="/wiki/Legume" title="Legume">legumes</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bean" title="Bean">beans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pea" title="Pea">peas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lentil" title="Lentil">lentils</a>, et cetera), and <a href="/wiki/Nut_(fruit)" title="Nut (fruit)">nuts</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oilseed" title="Oilseed">Oilseeds</a> are often pressed to produce rich oils - <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunflower" title="Sunflower">sunflower</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flaxseed" title="Flaxseed">flaxseed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rapeseed" title="Rapeseed">rapeseed</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Canola_oil" title="Canola oil">canola oil</a>), <a href="/wiki/Sesame" title="Sesame">sesame</a>, <a href="/wiki/Et_cetera" title="Et cetera">et cetera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McGee9_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-McGee9-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>Seeds are typically high in <a href="/wiki/Unsaturated_fat" title="Unsaturated fat">unsaturated fats</a> and, in moderation, are considered a <a href="/wiki/Health_food" title="Health food">health food</a>. However, not all seeds are edible. Large seeds, such as those from a <a href="/wiki/Lemon" title="Lemon">lemon</a>, pose a choking hazard, while seeds from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cherries" title="Cherries">cherries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Apple" title="Apple">apples</a>  contain <a href="/wiki/Cyanide" title="Cyanide">cyanide</a> which could be poisonous only if consumed in large volumes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">Fruits</a> are the ripened ovaries of plants, including the seeds within. Many plants and animals have <a href="/wiki/Coevolution" title="Coevolution">coevolved</a> such that the fruits of the former are an attractive food source to the latter, because animals that eat the fruits may <a href="/wiki/Excretion" title="Excretion">excrete</a> the seeds some distance away. Fruits, therefore, make up a significant part of the diets of most cultures. Some botanical fruits, such as <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pumpkin" title="Pumpkin">pumpkins</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eggplant" title="Eggplant">eggplants</a>, are eaten as vegetables.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> (For more information, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_fruits" title="List of fruits">list of fruits</a>.)
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Vegetable" title="Vegetable">Vegetables</a> are a second type of plant matter that is commonly eaten as food. These include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Root_vegetable" title="Root vegetable">root vegetables</a> (<a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carrot" title="Carrot">carrots</a>), bulbs (<a href="/wiki/Onion" title="Onion">onion</a> family), <a href="/wiki/Leaf_vegetable" title="Leaf vegetable">leaf vegetables</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spinach" title="Spinach">spinach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lettuce" title="Lettuce">lettuce</a>), <a href="/wiki/Category:Stem_vegetables" title="Category:Stem vegetables">stem vegetables</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bamboo" title="Bamboo">bamboo</a> shoots and <a href="/wiki/Asparagus" title="Asparagus">asparagus</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Category:Inflorescence_vegetables" title="Category:Inflorescence vegetables">inflorescence vegetables</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Globe_artichoke" title="Globe artichoke">globe artichokes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Broccoli" title="Broccoli">broccoli</a> and other vegetables such as <a href="/wiki/Cabbage" title="Cabbage">cabbage</a> or <a href="/wiki/Cauliflower" title="Cauliflower">cauliflower</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Animals">Animals</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Animal_source_foods" title="Animal source foods">Animal source foods</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_chain" title="Food chain">Food chain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meatfoodgroup.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="255" data-file-width="756" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Meatfoodgroup.jpg/330px-Meatfoodgroup.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Meatfoodgroup.jpg/495px-Meatfoodgroup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Meatfoodgroup.jpg/660px-Meatfoodgroup.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meatfoodgroup.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Various raw <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">meats</a></div></div></div>
<p>Animals are used as food either directly or indirectly by the products they produce. <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">Meat</a> is an example of a direct product taken from an animal, which comes from <a href="/wiki/Muscle" title="Muscle">muscle</a> systems or from <a href="/wiki/Organ_(anatomy)" title="Organ (anatomy)">organs</a>.
</p><p>Food products produced by animals include <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a> produced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mammary_glands" title="Mammary glands">mammary glands</a>, which in many cultures is drunk or processed into <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy products</a> (cheese, butter, etc.). In addition, birds and other animals lay <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egg_(food)" title="Egg (food)">eggs</a>, which are often eaten, and <a href="/wiki/Bee" title="Bee">bees</a> produce <a href="/wiki/Honey" title="Honey">honey</a>, a reduced <a href="/wiki/Nectar" title="Nectar">nectar</a> from flowers, which is a popular sweetener in many cultures. Some cultures <a href="/wiki/Blood_as_food" title="Blood as food">consume blood</a>, sometimes in the form of <a href="/wiki/Blood_sausage" title="Blood sausage">blood sausage</a>, as a thickener for sauces, or in a <a href="/wiki/Curing_(food_preservation)" title="Curing (food preservation)">cured</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salting_(food)" title="Salting (food)">salted</a> form for times of food scarcity, and others use <a href="/wiki/Blood" title="Blood">blood</a> in stews such as <a href="/wiki/Jugging" title="Jugging">jugged hare</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some cultures and people do not consume meat or animal food products for cultural, dietary, health, ethical, or ideological reasons. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vegetarian" title="Vegetarian">Vegetarians</a> choose to forgo food from animal sources to varying degrees. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vegan" title="Vegan">Vegans</a> do not consume any foods that are or contain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ingredients" title="Ingredients">ingredients</a> from an animal source.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ueberladewagen_(jha).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="710" data-file-width="1094" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg/220px-Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg/330px-Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg/440px-Ueberladewagen_%28jha%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ueberladewagen_(jha).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Tractor" title="Tractor">tractor</a> pulling a <a href="/wiki/Chaser_bin" title="Chaser bin">chaser bin</a></div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">Food industry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Genetically_modified_food" title="Genetically modified food">Genetically modified food</a></div>
<p>Most food has always been obtained through <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>. With increasing concern over both the methods and products of modern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_agriculture" title="Industrial agriculture">industrial agriculture</a>, there has been a growing trend toward <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_agriculture" title="Sustainable agriculture">sustainable agricultural</a> practices. This approach, partly fueled by consumer demand, encourages <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>, local self-reliance and <a href="/wiki/Organic_farming" title="Organic farming">organic farming</a> methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Major influences on food production include international organizations (e.g. the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a>), national government policy (or law), and war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Messer_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Messer-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>In popular culture, the mass production of food, specifically meats such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicken_(food)" title="Chicken (food)">chicken</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, has come under fire from various <a href="/wiki/Documentary_film" title="Documentary film">documentaries</a>, most recently <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food,_Inc" title="Food, Inc">Food, Inc</a>, documenting the mass slaughter and poor treatment of animals, often for easier revenues from <a href="/wiki/Corporate_farming" title="Corporate farming">large corporations</a>. Along with a current trend towards <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a>, people in <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western culture</a> have had an increasing trend towards the use of <a href="/wiki/Herbalism" title="Herbalism">herbal supplements</a>, foods for a specific group of people (such as dieters, women, or athletes), <a href="/wiki/Functional_food" title="Functional food">functional foods</a> (fortified foods, such as omega-3 eggs), and a more ethnically diverse diet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>Several organisations have begun calling for a new kind of agriculture in which <a href="/wiki/Agroecosystem" title="Agroecosystem">agroecosystems</a> provide food but also support vital <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystem</a> services so that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertility_(soil)" title="Fertility (soil)">soil fertility</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> are maintained rather than compromised. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Water_Management_Institute" title="International Water Management Institute">International Water Management Institute</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNEP" title="UNEP">UNEP</a>, well-managed agroecosystems not only provide food, fiber and animal products, they also provide services such as <a href="/wiki/Flood_mitigation" title="Flood mitigation">flood mitigation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Groundwater_recharge" title="Groundwater recharge">groundwater recharge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erosion_control" title="Erosion control">erosion control</a> and habitats for plants, birds, fish and other animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Taste_perception">Taste perception</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Taste" title="Taste">Taste</a></div>
<p>Animals, specifically humans, have five different types of tastes: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet" title="Sweet">sweet</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sour" title="Sour">sour</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saltiness" title="Saltiness">salty</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bitter_(taste)" title="Bitter (taste)">bitter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Umami" title="Umami">umami</a>. As animals have <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolved</a>, the tastes that provide the most energy (<a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fat" title="Fat">fats</a>) are the most pleasant to eat while others, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bitter_(taste)" title="Bitter (taste)">bitter</a>, are not enjoyable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Water, while important for survival, has no taste.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Fats, on the other hand, especially <a href="/wiki/Saturated_fat" title="Saturated fat">saturated fats</a>, are thicker and rich and are thus considered more enjoyable to eat.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweet">Sweet</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saccharose2.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="178" data-file-width="345" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Saccharose2.svg/200px-Saccharose2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Saccharose2.svg/300px-Saccharose2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Saccharose2.svg/400px-Saccharose2.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saccharose2.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Structure of sucrose</div></div></div>
<p>Generally regarded as the most pleasant taste, <a href="/wiki/Sweetness" title="Sweetness">sweetness</a> is almost always caused by a type of simple <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Glucose" title="Glucose">glucose</a> or <a href="/wiki/Fructose" title="Fructose">fructose</a>, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disaccharides" title="Disaccharides">disaccharides</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Sucrose" title="Sucrose">sucrose</a>, a molecule combining glucose and fructose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Oxford_American_Dictionary_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_Oxford_American_Dictionary-19">[19]</a></sup> Complex carbohydrates are long chains and thus do not have the sweet taste. Artificial sweeteners such as <a href="/wiki/Sucralose" title="Sucralose">sucralose</a> are used to mimic the sugar molecule, creating the sensation of sweet, without the calories. Other types of sugar include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raw_sugar" title="Raw sugar">raw sugar</a>, which is known for its amber color, as it is unprocessed. As sugar is vital for energy and survival, the taste of sugar is pleasant.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Stevia" title="Stevia">stevia</a> plant contains a compound known as <a href="/wiki/Steviol" title="Steviol">steviol</a> which, when extracted, has 300 times the sweetness of sugar while having minimal impact on blood sugar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sour">Sour</span></h3>
<p>Sourness is caused by the taste of <a href="/wiki/Acid" title="Acid">acids</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Vinegar" title="Vinegar">vinegar</a> in alcoholic beverages. Sour foods include <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus</a>, specifically <a href="/wiki/Lemon" title="Lemon">lemons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lime_(fruit)" title="Lime (fruit)">limes</a>, and to a lesser degree <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">oranges</a>. Sour is evolutionarily significant as it is a sign for a food that may have gone <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rancidity" title="Rancidity">rancid</a> due to bacteria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Many foods, however, are slightly acidic, and help stimulate the taste buds and enhance flavor.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Salty">Salty</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Piles_of_Salt_Salar_de_Uyuni_Bolivia_Luca_Galuzzi_2006_a.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1320" data-file-width="2000" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Piles_of_Salt_Salar_de_Uyuni_Bolivia_Luca_Galuzzi_2006_a.jpg/220px-Piles_of_Salt_Salar_de_Uyuni_Bolivia_Luca_Galuzzi_2006_a.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Piles_of_Salt_Salar_de_Uyuni_Bolivia_Luca_Galuzzi_2006_a.jpg/330px-Piles_of_Salt_Salar_de_Uyuni_Bolivia_Luca_Galuzzi_2006_a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Piles_of_Salt_Salar_de_Uyuni_Bolivia_Luca_Galuzzi_2006_a.jpg/440px-Piles_of_Salt_Salar_de_Uyuni_Bolivia_Luca_Galuzzi_2006_a.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Piles_of_Salt_Salar_de_Uyuni_Bolivia_Luca_Galuzzi_2006_a.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Salt mounds in <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a></div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saltiness" title="Saltiness">Saltiness</a> is the taste of <a href="/wiki/Alkali_metal" title="Alkali metal">alkali metal</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ions" title="Ions">ions</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Sodium" title="Sodium">sodium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Potassium" title="Potassium">potassium</a>. It is found in almost every food in low to moderate proportions to enhance flavor, although to eat pure salt is regarded as highly unpleasant. There are many different types of salt, with each having a different degree of saltiness, including <a href="/wiki/Sea_salt" title="Sea salt">sea salt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fleur_de_sel" title="Fleur de sel">fleur de sel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosher_salt" title="Kosher salt">kosher salt</a>, mined salt, and grey salt. Other than enhancing flavor, its significance is that the body needs and maintains a delicate <a href="/wiki/Electrolyte" title="Electrolyte">electrolyte</a> balance, which is the <a href="/wiki/Kidney" title="Kidney">kidney</a>'s function. Salt may be iodized, meaning <a href="/wiki/Iodine" title="Iodine">iodine</a> has been added to it, a necessary nutrient that promotes <a href="/wiki/Thyroid" title="Thyroid">thyroid</a> function. Some canned foods, notably <a href="/wiki/Soup" title="Soup">soups</a> or packaged <a href="/wiki/Broth" title="Broth">broths</a>, tend to be high in salt as a means of preserving the food longer. Historically salt has long been used as a meat preservative as salt promotes water excretion. Similarly, dried foods also promote food safety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bitter">Bitter</span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bitter_(taste)" title="Bitter (taste)">Bitterness</a> is a sensation often considered unpleasant characterized by having a sharp, pungent taste. Unsweetened dark <a href="/wiki/Chocolate" title="Chocolate">chocolate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caffeine" title="Caffeine">caffeine</a>, lemon rind, and some types of fruit are known to be bitter.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Umami">Umami</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Umami" title="Umami">Umami</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a> word for delicious, is the least known in Western popular culture but has a long tradition in Asian cuisine. Umami is the taste of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glutamate" title="Glutamate">glutamates</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Monosodium_glutamate" title="Monosodium glutamate">monosodium glutamate</a> (MSG).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Oxford_American_Dictionary_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-New_Oxford_American_Dictionary-19">[19]</a></sup> It is characterized as savory, meaty, and rich in flavor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">Salmon</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mushrooms" title="Mushrooms">mushrooms</a> are foods high in umami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine" title="Cuisine">Cuisine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regional_cuisine" title="Regional cuisine">Regional cuisine</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_cuisines" title="Global cuisines">Global cuisines</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bali_cuisine.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Bali_cuisine.jpg/220px-Bali_cuisine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Bali_cuisine.jpg/330px-Bali_cuisine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Bali_cuisine.jpg/440px-Bali_cuisine.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bali_cuisine.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Typical <a href="/wiki/Balinese_cuisine" title="Balinese cuisine">Balinese cuisine</a> in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a></div></div></div>
<p>Many scholars claim that the rhetorical function of food is to represent the culture of a country, and that it can be used as a form of communication. According to Goode, Curtis and Theophano, food "is the last aspect of an ethnic culture to be lost".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many cultures have a recognizable cuisine, a specific set of <a href="/wiki/Cooking" title="Cooking">cooking</a> traditions using various spices or a combination of flavors unique to that culture, which evolves over time. Other differences include preferences (hot or cold, spicy, etc.) and practices, the study of which is known as <a href="/wiki/Gastronomy" title="Gastronomy">gastronomy</a>. Many cultures have diversified their foods by means of preparation, cooking methods, and manufacturing. This also includes a complex food trade which helps the cultures to economically survive by way of food, not just by consumption.
</p><p>Some popular types of ethnic foods include <a href="/wiki/Italian_cuisine" title="Italian cuisine">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_cuisine" title="French cuisine">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_cuisine" title="Japanese cuisine">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cuisine" title="Chinese cuisine">Chinese</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_United_States" title="Cuisine of the United States">American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cajun_cuisine" title="Cajun cuisine">Cajun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thai_cuisine" title="Thai cuisine">Thai</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_cuisine" title="African cuisine">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_cuisine" title="Indian cuisine">Indian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nepalese_cuisine" title="Nepalese cuisine">Nepalese</a>. Various cultures throughout the world study the dietary analysis of food <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habit_(psychology)" title="Habit (psychology)">habits</a>. While <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolutionarily</a> speaking, as opposed to culturally, humans are <a href="/wiki/Omnivore" title="Omnivore">omnivores</a>, religion and social constructs such as <a href="/wiki/Morality" title="Morality">morality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Activism" title="Activism">activism</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a> will often affect which foods they will consume. Food is eaten and typically enjoyed through the sense of <a href="/wiki/Taste" title="Taste">taste</a>, the perception of flavor from eating and drinking. Certain tastes are more enjoyable than others, for evolutionary purposes.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Presentation">Presentation</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG/220px-Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG/330px-Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG/440px-Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> basil salmon <a href="/wiki/Terrine_(food)" title="Terrine (food)">terrine</a>, with eye-appealing <a href="/wiki/Garnish_(food)" title="Garnish (food)">garnishes</a></div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Food_presentation" title="Food presentation">Food presentation</a></div>
<p>Aesthetically pleasing and eye-appealing food presentations can encourage people to consume foods. A common saying is that people "eat with their eyes". Food presented in a clean and appetizing way will encourage a good flavor, even if unsatisfactory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Food_Texture,_Andrew_J._Rosenthal_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Food_Texture,_Andrew_J._Rosenthal-27">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contrast_in_texture">Contrast in texture</span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texture_(food)" title="Texture (food)">Texture</a> plays a crucial role in the enjoyment of eating foods. Contrasts in textures, such as something crunchy in an otherwise smooth dish, may increase the appeal of eating it. Common examples include adding <a href="/wiki/Granola" title="Granola">granola</a> to <a href="/wiki/Yogurt" title="Yogurt">yogurt</a>, adding <a href="/wiki/Crouton" title="Crouton">croutons</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Salad" title="Salad">salad</a> or <a href="/wiki/Soup" title="Soup">soup</a>, and toasting bread to enhance its crunchiness for a smooth topping, such as jam or butter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contrast_in_taste">Contrast in taste</span></h3>
<p>Another universal phenomenon regarding food is the appeal of contrast in taste and presentation. For example, such opposite flavors as <a href="/wiki/Sweetness" title="Sweetness">sweetness</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saltiness" title="Saltiness">saltiness</a> tend to go well together, as in <a href="/wiki/Kettle_corn" title="Kettle corn">kettle corn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nut_(fruit)" title="Nut (fruit)">nuts</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_preparation">Food preparation</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_food_preparation" title="Outline of food preparation">Outline of food preparation</a></div>
<p>While many foods can be eaten raw, many also undergo some form of preparation for reasons of safety, <a href="/wiki/Palatability" title="Palatability">palatability</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mouthfeel" title="Mouthfeel">texture</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Flavor" title="Flavor">flavor</a>. At the simplest level this may involve washing, cutting, trimming, or adding other foods or ingredients, such as spices. It may also involve mixing, heating or cooling, <a href="/wiki/Pressure_cooking" title="Pressure cooking">pressure cooking</a>, fermentation, or combination with other food. In a home, most food preparation takes place in a <a href="/wiki/Kitchen" title="Kitchen">kitchen</a>. Some preparation is done to enhance the <a href="/wiki/Taste" title="Taste">taste</a> or aesthetic appeal; other preparation may help to <a href="/wiki/Food_preservation" title="Food preservation">preserve</a> the food; others may be involved in cultural identity. A <a href="/wiki/Meal" title="Meal">meal</a> is made up of food which is prepared to be eaten at a specific time and place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LG_refrigerator_interior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/LG_refrigerator_interior.jpg/220px-LG_refrigerator_interior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/LG_refrigerator_interior.jpg/330px-LG_refrigerator_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/LG_refrigerator_interior.jpg/440px-LG_refrigerator_interior.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LG_refrigerator_interior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A refrigerator helps to keep foods fresh.</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Animal_preparation">Animal preparation</span></h4>
<p>The preparation of animal-based food usually involves <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slaughter_(livestock)" title="Slaughter (livestock)">slaughter</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evisceration_(organ_removal)" title="Evisceration (organ removal)">evisceration</a>, hanging, portioning, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rendering_(food_processing)" title="Rendering (food processing)">rendering</a>. In developed countries, this is usually done outside the home in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slaughterhouses" title="Slaughterhouses">slaughterhouses</a>, which are used to process animals en masse for meat production. Many countries regulate their slaughterhouses by law. For example, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> has established the <a href="/wiki/Humane_Slaughter_Act" title="Humane Slaughter Act">Humane Slaughter Act</a> of 1958, which requires that an animal be stunned before killing. This act, like those in many countries, exempts slaughter in accordance to religious law, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kosher" title="Kosher">kosher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shechita" title="Shechita">shechita</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dhab%C4%AB%E1%B8%A5ah" title="Dhabīḥah">dhabīḥah</a> halal. Strict interpretations of <a href="/wiki/Kashrut" title="Kashrut">kashrut</a> require the animal to be fully aware when its carotid artery is cut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p><p>On the local level, a butcher may commonly break down larger animal meat into smaller manageable cuts, and pre-wrap them for commercial sale or wrap them to order in butcher paper. In addition, fish and <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">seafood</a> may be fabricated into smaller cuts by a fish monger. However, fish butchery may be done on board a fishing vessel and quick-frozen for preservation of quality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooking">Cooking</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wok_cooking_and_the_heat_source_by_The_Pocket_in_Nanjing.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Wok_cooking_and_the_heat_source_by_The_Pocket_in_Nanjing.jpg/200px-Wok_cooking_and_the_heat_source_by_The_Pocket_in_Nanjing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Wok_cooking_and_the_heat_source_by_The_Pocket_in_Nanjing.jpg/300px-Wok_cooking_and_the_heat_source_by_The_Pocket_in_Nanjing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Wok_cooking_and_the_heat_source_by_The_Pocket_in_Nanjing.jpg/400px-Wok_cooking_and_the_heat_source_by_The_Pocket_in_Nanjing.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wok_cooking_and_the_heat_source_by_The_Pocket_in_Nanjing.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cooking with a <a href="/wiki/Wok" title="Wok">wok</a> in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a></div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cooking" title="Cooking">Cooking</a></div>
<p>The term "cooking" encompasses a vast range of methods, tools, and combinations of ingredients to improve the flavor or digestibility of food. Cooking technique, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Culinary_art" title="Culinary art">culinary art</a>, generally requires the selection, measurement, and combining of ingredients in an ordered procedure in an effort to achieve the desired result. Constraints on success include the variability of ingredients, ambient conditions, <a href="/wiki/Tool" title="Tool">tools</a>, and the skill of the individual cook.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The diversity of cooking worldwide is a reflection of the myriad nutritional, aesthetic, agricultural, economic, cultural, and religious considerations that affect it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silhnc_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-silhnc-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cooking requires applying heat to a food which usually, though not always, chemically changes the molecules, thus changing its flavor, <a href="/wiki/Mouthfeel" title="Mouthfeel">texture</a>, appearance, and nutritional properties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Cooking certain proteins, such as egg whites, meats, and fish, denatures the protein, causing it to firm. There is archaeological evidence of roasted foodstuffs at <i><a href="/wiki/Homo_erectus" title="Homo erectus">Homo erectus</a></i> campsites dating from 420,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Boiling as a means of cooking requires a container, and has been practiced at least since the 10th millennium BC with the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Pottery" title="Pottery">pottery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooking_equipment">Cooking equipment</span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pfanne_(Edelstahl).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="409" data-file-width="520" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Pfanne_%28Edelstahl%29.jpg/220px-Pfanne_%28Edelstahl%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Pfanne_%28Edelstahl%29.jpg/330px-Pfanne_%28Edelstahl%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Pfanne_%28Edelstahl%29.jpg/440px-Pfanne_%28Edelstahl%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pfanne_(Edelstahl).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Stainless_steel" title="Stainless steel">stainless steel</a> <a href="/wiki/Frying_pan" title="Frying pan">frying pan</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TraditionalAsado.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/TraditionalAsado.jpg/220px-TraditionalAsado.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/TraditionalAsado.jpg/330px-TraditionalAsado.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/TraditionalAsado.jpg/440px-TraditionalAsado.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TraditionalAsado.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A traditional <a href="/wiki/Asado" title="Asado">asado</a> (barbecue)</div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cookware_and_bakeware" title="Cookware and bakeware">Cookware and bakeware</a></div>
<p>There are many different types of equipment used for cooking.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Oven" title="Oven">Ovens</a> are mostly hollow devices that get very hot (up to 500 °F (260 °C)) and are used for baking or roasting and offer a dry-heat cooking method. Different cuisines will use different types of ovens. For example, Indian culture uses a <a href="/wiki/Tandoor" title="Tandoor">tandoor</a> oven, which is a cylindrical clay oven which operates at a single high temperature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Western kitchens use variable temperature <a href="/wiki/Convection_oven" title="Convection oven">convection ovens</a>, conventional ovens, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toaster_oven" title="Toaster oven">toaster ovens</a>, or non-radiant heat ovens like the <a href="/wiki/Microwave_oven" title="Microwave oven">microwave oven</a>. Classic Italian cuisine includes the use of a brick oven containing burning wood. Ovens may be wood-fired, coal-fired, <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">gas</a>, electric, or oil-fired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>Various types of cook-tops are used as well. They carry the same variations of fuel types as the ovens mentioned above. Cook-tops are used to heat vessels placed on top of the heat source, such as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saut%C3%A9_pan" title="Sauté pan">sauté pan</a>, sauce pot, <a href="/wiki/Frying_pan" title="Frying pan">frying pan</a>, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pressure_cooker" title="Pressure cooker">pressure cooker</a>. These pieces of equipment can use either a moist or dry cooking method and include methods such as <a href="/wiki/Steam" title="Steam">steaming</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Simmer" title="Simmer">simmering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boiling" title="Boiling">boiling</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Poaching_(cooking)" title="Poaching (cooking)">poaching</a> for moist methods, while the dry methods include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saut%C3%A9" title="Sauté">sautéing</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pan_fry" title="Pan fry">pan frying</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deep-fry" title="Deep-fry">deep-frying</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition, many cultures use grills for cooking. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grill_(cooking)" title="Grill (cooking)">grill</a> operates with a radiant heat source from below, usually covered with a metal grid and sometimes a cover. An open pit barbecue in the American south is one example along with the American style outdoor grill fueled by wood, liquid propane, or charcoal along with soaked wood chips for smoking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Mexican_cuisine" title="Mexican cuisine">Mexican</a> style of barbecue is called <a href="/wiki/Barbacoa" title="Barbacoa">barbacoa</a>, which involves the cooking of meats such as whole sheep over an open fire. In <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Asado" title="Asado">asado</a> (Spanish for "grilled") is prepared on a grill held over an open pit or fire made upon the ground, on which a whole animal or smaller cuts are grilled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Raw_food_preparation">Raw food preparation<span id="Raw_Food_Preparation"></span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2007feb-sushi-odaiba-manytypes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="3072" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/2007feb-sushi-odaiba-manytypes.jpg/220px-2007feb-sushi-odaiba-manytypes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/2007feb-sushi-odaiba-manytypes.jpg/330px-2007feb-sushi-odaiba-manytypes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/2007feb-sushi-odaiba-manytypes.jpg/440px-2007feb-sushi-odaiba-manytypes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2007feb-sushi-odaiba-manytypes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Many types of <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> ready to be eaten, including <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">tuna</a></div></div></div>
<p>Certain cultures highlight animal and vegetable foods in a <a href="/wiki/Raw_foodism" title="Raw foodism">raw state</a>. <a href="/wiki/Salad" title="Salad">Salads</a> consisting of raw vegetables or fruits are common in many cuisines. <a href="/wiki/Sashimi" title="Sashimi">Sashimi</a> in <a href="/wiki/Japanese_cuisine" title="Japanese cuisine">Japanese cuisine</a> consists of raw sliced <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> or other meat, and <a href="/wiki/Sushi" title="Sushi">sushi</a> often incorporates raw fish or seafood. <a href="/wiki/Steak_tartare" title="Steak tartare">Steak tartare</a> and salmon tartare are dishes made from diced or ground raw beef or salmon, mixed with various ingredients and served with <a href="/wiki/Baguette" title="Baguette">baguettes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brioche" title="Brioche">brioche</a>, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frites" title="Frites">frites</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In Italy, <a href="/wiki/Carpaccio" title="Carpaccio">carpaccio</a> is a dish of very thinly sliced raw <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, drizzled with a <a href="/wiki/Vinaigrette" title="Vinaigrette">vinaigrette</a> made with olive oil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The health food movement known as <a href="/wiki/Raw_foodism" title="Raw foodism">raw foodism</a> promotes a mostly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vegan" title="Vegan">vegan</a> diet of raw fruits, vegetables, and grains prepared in various ways, including juicing, food dehydration, sprouting, and other methods of preparation that do not heat the food above 118 °F (47.8 °C).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> An example of a raw meat dish is <a href="/wiki/Ceviche" title="Ceviche">ceviche</a>, a Latin American dish made with raw meat that is "cooked" from the highly acidic citric juice from lemons and limes along with other aromatics such as garlic.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Restaurants">Restaurants</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Inside_Le_Procope.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="954" data-file-width="1280" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Inside_Le_Procope.jpg/220px-Inside_Le_Procope.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Inside_Le_Procope.jpg/330px-Inside_Le_Procope.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Inside_Le_Procope.jpg/440px-Inside_Le_Procope.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Inside_Le_Procope.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_Procope" title="Café Procope">Café Procope</a> in Paris was founded in 1686</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Allyn_House_restaurant_menu_(March_5,_1859).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Allyn_House_restaurant_menu_%28March_5%2C_1859%29.jpg/220px-Allyn_House_restaurant_menu_%28March_5%2C_1859%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Allyn_House_restaurant_menu_%28March_5%2C_1859%29.jpg/330px-Allyn_House_restaurant_menu_%28March_5%2C_1859%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Allyn_House_restaurant_menu_%28March_5%2C_1859%29.jpg/440px-Allyn_House_restaurant_menu_%28March_5%2C_1859%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Allyn_House_restaurant_menu_(March_5,_1859).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Allyn House restaurant menu (March 5, 1859)</div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Restaurant" title="Restaurant">Restaurant</a></div>
<p>Restaurants employ <a href="/wiki/Chef" title="Chef">chefs</a> to prepare the food, and <a href="/wiki/Waiting_staff" title="Waiting staff">waiters</a> to serve customers at the table.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The term restaurant comes from an old term for a restorative <a href="/wiki/Broth" title="Broth">meat broth</a>; this broth (or bouillon) was served in elegant outlets in Paris from the mid 18th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-history-47">[47]</a></sup> These refined "restaurants" were a marked change from the usual basic eateries such as inns and taverns,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-history-47">[47]</a></sup> and some had developed from early <a href="/wiki/Parisian_caf%C3%A9" title="Parisian café">Parisian cafés</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_Procope" title="Café Procope">Café Procope</a>, by first serving bouillon, then adding other cooked food to their menus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>Commercial eateries existed during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_period" title="Roman period">Roman period</a>, with evidence of 150 "thermopolia", a form of fast food restaurant, found in <a href="/wiki/Pompeii" title="Pompeii">Pompeii</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> and urban sales of prepared foods may have existed in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song dynasty</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In 2005, the population of the United States spent $496 billion on out-of-home <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dining" title="Dining">dining</a>. Expenditures by type of out-of-home dining were as follows: 40% in full-service restaurants, 37.2% in limited service restaurants (<a href="/wiki/Fast_food" title="Fast food">fast food</a>), 6.6% in schools or colleges, 5.4% in bars and <a href="/wiki/Vending_machine" title="Vending machine">vending machines</a>, 4.7% in hotels and motels, 4.0% in recreational places, and 2.2% in others, which includes military bases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Template:Refexample#Self-sourcing" title="Template:Refexample"><span title="This example needs references to sources that describe its significance in the context of the article. (October 2018)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Stay_on_topic" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles"><span title="The material near this tag may contain information that is not relevant to the article's main topic. (October 2018)">relevant?</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:Food" title="Talk:Food">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_manufacturing">Food manufacturing</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Food_packages_(1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1524" data-file-width="2136" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Food_packages_%281%29.jpg/220px-Food_packages_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Food_packages_%281%29.jpg/330px-Food_packages_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Food_packages_%281%29.jpg/440px-Food_packages_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Food_packages_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Packaged household food items</div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_manufacture" title="Food manufacture">Food manufacture</a></div>
<p>Packaged foods are manufactured outside the home for purchase. This can be as simple as a <a href="/wiki/Butcher" title="Butcher">butcher</a> preparing meat, or as complex as a modern international <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">food industry</a>. Early food processing techniques were limited by available food preservation, packaging, and transportation. This mainly involved <a href="/wiki/Salting_(food)" title="Salting (food)">salting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curing_(food_preservation)" title="Curing (food preservation)">curing</a>, curdling, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drying_(food)" title="Drying (food)">drying</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pickling" title="Pickling">pickling</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fermentation_(food)" title="Fermentation (food)">fermenting</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smoking_(food)" title="Smoking (food)">smoking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Food manufacturing arose during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" title="Industrial revolution">industrial revolution</a> in the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> This development took advantage of new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mass-marketing" title="Mass-marketing">mass markets</a> and emerging technology, such as <a href="/wiki/Mill_(grinding)" title="Mill (grinding)">milling</a>, preservation, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Packaging" title="Packaging">packaging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Packaging_and_labeling" title="Packaging and labeling">labeling</a>, and transportation. It brought the advantages of pre-prepared time-saving food to the bulk of ordinary people who did not employ domestic servants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jango_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jango-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the start of the 21st century, a two-tier structure has arisen, with a few international food processing giants controlling a wide range of well-known food <a href="/wiki/Brand" title="Brand">brands</a>. There also exists a wide array of small local or national food processing companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Advanced technologies have also come to change food manufacture. Computer-based control systems, sophisticated <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">processing</a> and packaging methods, and <a href="/wiki/Logistics" title="Logistics">logistics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Food_distribution" title="Food distribution">distribution</a> advances can enhance product quality, improve <a href="/wiki/Food_safety" title="Food safety">food safety</a>, and reduce costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jango_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jango-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_trade">Commercial trade</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="717" data-file-width="1434" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png/220px-Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png/330px-Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png/440px-Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seawifs_global_biosphere_2002.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/SeaWiFS" title="SeaWiFS">SeaWiFS</a> image for the global biosphere</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Food_consumption.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" height="96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Food_consumption.gif/220px-Food_consumption.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Food_consumption.gif/330px-Food_consumption.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Food_consumption.gif/440px-Food_consumption.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Food_consumption.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Global average daily <a href="/wiki/Calorie" title="Calorie">calorie</a> consumption in 1995</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2005food_import.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" height="96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/2005food_import.png/220px-2005food_import.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/2005food_import.png/330px-2005food_import.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/2005food_import.png/440px-2005food_import.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2005food_import.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Food <a href="/wiki/Import" title="Import">imports</a> in 2005</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Population_density_countries_2017_world_map,_people_per_sq_km.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="864" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Population_density_countries_2017_world_map%2C_people_per_sq_km.svg/220px-Population_density_countries_2017_world_map%2C_people_per_sq_km.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Population_density_countries_2017_world_map%2C_people_per_sq_km.svg/330px-Population_density_countries_2017_world_map%2C_people_per_sq_km.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Population_density_countries_2017_world_map%2C_people_per_sq_km.svg/440px-Population_density_countries_2017_world_map%2C_people_per_sq_km.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Population_density_countries_2017_world_map,_people_per_sq_km.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">Population density</a> by country</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_food_imports_and_exports">International food imports and exports</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">Population density</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> reported that the European Union was the top food importer in 2005, followed at a distance by the USA and Japan. <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a>'s need for food was especially well illustrated in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.  Despite the implementation of <a href="/wiki/Rationing_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Rationing in the United Kingdom">food rationing</a>, Britain remained dependent on food imports and the result was a long term engagement in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Atlantic" title="Battle of the Atlantic">Battle of the Atlantic</a>.
</p><p>Food is traded and marketed on a global basis. The variety and availability of food is no longer restricted by the diversity of locally grown food or the limitations of the local growing season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Between 1961 and 1999, there was a 400% increase in worldwide food exports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Some countries are now economically dependent on food exports, which in some cases account for over 80% of all exports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1994, over 100 countries became signatories to the <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_Round" title="Uruguay Round">Uruguay Round</a> of the <a href="/wiki/General_Agreement_on_Tariffs_and_Trade" title="General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade">General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade</a> in a dramatic increase in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_liberalization" title="Trade liberalization">trade liberalization</a>. This included an agreement to reduce subsidies paid to farmers, underpinned by the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a> enforcement of <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_policy" title="Agricultural policy">agricultural subsidy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tax,_tariff_and_trade" title="Tax, tariff and trade">tariffs</a>, import <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quota_Share" title="Quota Share">quotas</a>, and settlement of trade disputes that cannot be bilaterally resolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Where trade barriers are raised on the disputed grounds of public health and safety, the WTO refer the dispute to the <a href="/wiki/Codex_Alimentarius" title="Codex Alimentarius">Codex Alimentarius</a> Commission, which was founded in 1962 by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a> and the World Health Organization. Trade liberalization has greatly affected world food trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing_and_retailing">Marketing and retailing</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1835" data-file-width="2790" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg/260px-Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg/390px-Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg/520px-Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fredmeyer_edit_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Packaged food aisles of supermarket in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States of America</a></div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Food_marketing" title="Food marketing">Food marketing</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Food_marketing" title="Food marketing">Food marketing</a> brings together the producer and the consumer. The marketing of even a single food product can be a complicated process involving many producers and companies. For example, fifty-six companies are involved in making one <a href="/wiki/Canning" title="Canning">can</a> of chicken noodle soup. These businesses include not only chicken and vegetable processors but also the companies that transport the ingredients and those who print labels and manufacture cans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The food marketing system is the largest direct and indirect non-government employer in the United States.
</p><p>In the pre-modern era, the sale of surplus food took place once a week when farmers took their wares on market day into the local village marketplace. Here food was sold to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grocer" title="Grocer">grocers</a> for sale in their local shops for purchase by local consumers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silhnc_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-silhnc-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jango_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jango-53">[53]</a></sup> With the onset of industrialization and the development of the food processing industry, a wider range of food could be sold and distributed in distant locations. Typically early grocery shops would be counter-based shops, in which purchasers told the shop-keeper what they wanted, so that the shop-keeper could get it for them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silhnc_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-silhnc-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 20th century, <a href="/wiki/Supermarket" title="Supermarket">supermarkets</a> were born. Supermarkets brought with them a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self_service" title="Self service">self service</a> approach to shopping using <a href="/wiki/Shopping_cart" title="Shopping cart">shopping carts</a>, and were able to offer quality food at lower cost through <a href="/wiki/Economies_of_scale" title="Economies of scale">economies of scale</a> and reduced staffing costs. In the latter part of the 20th century, this has been further revolutionized by the development of vast warehouse-sized, out-of-town supermarkets, selling a wide range of food from around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>Unlike food processors, food retailing is a two-tier market in which a small number of very large <a href="/wiki/Corporation" title="Corporation">companies</a> control a large proportion of supermarkets. The supermarket giants wield great purchasing power over farmers and processors, and strong influence over consumers. Nevertheless, less than 10% of consumer spending on food goes to farmers, with larger percentages going to <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">advertising</a>, transportation, and intermediate corporations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prices">Prices</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GrainProducts.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2790" data-file-width="1867" height="329" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/GrainProducts.jpg/220px-GrainProducts.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/GrainProducts.jpg/330px-GrainProducts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/GrainProducts.jpg/440px-GrainProducts.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GrainProducts.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Some essential food products including <a href="/wiki/Bread" title="Bread">bread</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pasta" title="Pasta">pasta</a></div></div></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Food_vs._fuel" title="Food vs. fuel">Food vs. fuel</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Annual_real_food_price_indices.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="370" data-file-width="760" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Annual_real_food_price_indices.svg/220px-Annual_real_food_price_indices.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Annual_real_food_price_indices.svg/330px-Annual_real_food_price_indices.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Annual_real_food_price_indices.svg/440px-Annual_real_food_price_indices.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Annual_real_food_price_indices.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Food, meat, dairy, cereals, vegetable oil, and sugar price indices, deflated using the World Bank Manufactures Unit Value Index (MUV)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>It is rare for price spikes to hit all major foods in most countries at once, but <a href="/wiki/Food_prices" title="Food prices">food prices</a> suffered all-time peaks in 2008 and 2011, posting a 15% and 12% deflated increase year-over-year, representing prices higher than any data collected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2007, 37 countries faced food crises, and 20 had imposed some sort of food-price controls. In China, the price of <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a> jumped 58% in 2007. In the 1980s and 1990s, farm subsidies and support programs allowed major grain exporting countries to hold large surpluses, which could be tapped during food shortages to keep prices down. However, new trade policies had made agricultural production much more responsive to market demands, putting global food reserves at their lowest since 1983.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn24march2008_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn24march2008-66">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>Rising food prices in those years have been linked with social unrest around the world, including rioting in <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ind_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ind-67">[67]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>
Food prices worldwide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932008_world_food_price_crisis" title="2007–2008 world food price crisis">increased in 2008</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>
One cause of rising food prices is wealthier Asian consumers are westernizing their diets, and farmers and nations of the third world are struggling to keep up the pace.
